buildQueueingHintMap(ctx context.Context, es []framework.EnqueueExtensions) (internalqueue.QueueingHintMap, error) {\n   395→\tqueueingHintMap := make(internalqueue.QueueingHintMap)\n   396→\tvar returnErr error\n   397→\tfor _, e := range es {\n   398→\t\tevents, err := e.EventsToRegister(ctx)\n   399→\t\tif err != nil {\n   400→\t\t\treturnErr = errors.Join(returnErr, err)\n   401→\t\t}\n   402→\n   403→\t\t// This will happen when plugin registers with empty events, it's usually the case a pod\n   404→\t\t// will become reschedulable only for self-update, e.g. schedulingGates plugin, the pod\n   405→\t\t// will enter into the activeQ via priorityQueue.Update().\n   406→\t\tif len(events) == 0 {\n   407→\t\t\tcontinue\n   408→\t\t}\n   409→\n   410→\t\t// Note: Rarely, a plugin implements EnqueueExtensions but returns nil.\n   411→\t\t// We treat it as: the plugin is not interested in any event, and hence pod failed by that plugin\n   412→\t\t// cannot be moved by any regular cluster event.\n   413→\t\t// So, we can just ignore such EventsToRegister here.\n   414→\n   415→\t\tregisterNodeAdded := false\n   416→\t\tregisterNodeTaintUpdated := false\n   417→\t\tfor _, event := range events {\n   418→\t\t\tfn := event.QueueingHintFn\n   419→\t\t\tif fn == nil || !utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.SchedulerQueueingHints) {\n   420→\t\t\t\tfn = defaultQueueingHintFn\n   421→\t\t\t}\n   422→\n   423→\t\t\tif event.Event.Resource == framework.Node {\n   424→\t\t\t\tif event.Event.ActionType&framework.Add != 0 {\n   425→\t\t\t\t\tregisterNodeAdded = true\n   426→\t\t\t\t}\n   427→\t\t\t\tif event.Event.ActionType&framework.UpdateNodeTaint != 0 {\n   428→\t\t\t\t\tregisterNodeTaintUpdated = true\n   429→\t\t\t\t}\n   430→\t\t\t}\n   431→\n   432→\t\t\tqueueingHintMap[event.Event] = append(queueingHintMap[event.Event], &internalqueue.QueueingHintFunction{\n   433→\t\t\t\tPluginName:     e.Name(),\n   434→\t\t\t\tQueueingHintFn: fn,\n   435→\t\t\t})\n   436→\t\t}\n   437→\t\tif registerNodeAdded && !registerNodeTaintUpdated {\n   438→\t\t\t// Temporally fix for the issue https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/109437\n   439→\t\t\t// NodeAdded QueueingHint isn't always called because of preCheck.\n   440→\t\t\t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\n   441→\t\t\t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\n   442→\t\t\t//\n   443→\t\t\t// So, here registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\n   444→\t\t\t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuch in the\n   445→\t\t\t// unschedulable pod pool.\n   446→\t\t\t// This behavior will be removed when we remove the preCheck feature.\n   447→\t\t\t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\n   448→\t\t\tqueueingHintMap[framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.UpdateNodeTaint}] =\n   449→\t\t\t\tappend(queueingHintMap[framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.UpdateNodeTaint}],\n   450→\t\t\t\t\t&internalqueue.QueueingHintFunction{\n   451→\t\t\t\t\t\tPluginName:     e.Name(),\n   452→\t\t\t\t\t\tQueueingHintFn: defaultQueueingHintFn,\n   453→\t\t\t\t\t},\n   454→\t\t\t\t)\n   455→\t\t}\n   456→\t}\n   457→\tif returnErr != nil {\n   458→\t\treturn nil, returnErr\n   459→\t}\n   460→\treturn queueingHintMap, nil\n   461→}\n   462→\n   463→// Run begins watching and scheduling. It starts scheduling and blocked until the context is done.\n   464→func (sched *Scheduler) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n   465→\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n   466→\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Run(logger)\n   467→\n   468→\t// We need to start scheduleOne loop in a dedicated goroutine,\n   469→\t// because scheduleOne function hangs on getting the next item\n   470→\t// from the SchedulingQueue.\n   471→\t// If there are no new pods to schedule, it will be hanging there\n   472→\t// and if done in this goroutine it will be blocking closing\n   473→\t// 547→\t\t}\n   548→\t}\n   549→\treturn fExtenders, nil\n   550→}\n   551→\n   552→type FailureHandlerFn func(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, podInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo, status watches for new unscheduled pods. It attempts to find\n// nodes that they fit on and writes bindings back to the api server.\ntype Scheduler struct {\n\t// It is expected that changes made via Cache will be observed\n\t// by NodeLister and Algorithm.\n\tCache internalcache.Cache\n\n\tExtenders []framework.Extender\n\n\t// NextPod should be a function that blocks until the next pod\n\t// is available. It watches for changes from\n  2383→// three channels (file, apiserver, and http) and creates a union of them. For\n  2384→// any new change seen, will run a sync against desired state and running state. If\n  2385→// no changes are seen to the configuration, will synchronize the last known desired\n  2386→// state every sync-frequency seconds. Never returns.\n  2387→func (kl *Kubelet) syncLoop(ctx context.Context, updates <-chan kubetypes.PodUpdate, handler SyncHandler) {\n  2388→\tklog.InfoS(\"Starting kubelet main sync loop\")\n  2389→\t// The syncTicker wakes up kubelet to checks if there are any pod workers\n  2390→\t// that need to be sync'd.
